# Excalidraw Data

## Text Elements
Why least squares (square error)? ^xO1LQY7l

Lets say for house price prediction:
Assume ^DhhXe1NX

"error" : unmodeled effects,
           random noise ^BfjN7IQU

ε is distributed as Gaussian would mean 0 and co-variance  σ squared. This means (Gaussian density): ^bJ39HSCU

0 ^NPAhi8pw

This implies ^qzKIAzcw

"parametrized by" ^zP2it3EY

variance ^lwtSMec4

mean ^uUjeaIEl

random 
variable y ^C8rMvEOL

I.e. ^V3UiM0T0

"likelihood of θ" ^wUFAPJxp

Whats the difference between likelihood of the parameters and probability of the data? They are the exactly same thing , but if you view this as a function of the parameters holding the data fixed and varying parameters θ, we call it likelihood. Whereas if you view the parameters θ as fixed and varying the data we say probability. ^oNjxXVnQ

MLE: maximum likelihood estimation.
    Choose θ to maximize L(θ). ^SDVmTfBw

"log likelihood" ^PsISu2mt

To simplify the algebra, rather than maximize L(θ), it is easier to maximize l(θ). ^BvylTccm

constant ^79lXpUyb

I.e. Choose θ to minimize ^SWvBSirB
